(2018).\nhttps://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005991\n\nUsing PhysiCell to test design rules for biorobots as a cancer treatment. \n\nHere, we construct two cell types as a bio-robotic cargo delivery system. \n\n1) \"Cargo\" cells secrete a chemoattractant to attract worker cells when they don't have cargo. They haul cargo chemotactically towards hypoxic regions. \n\nCancer cells (green) have a drug-induced damage model in this simulation, and undergo apoptosis at a rate proportional to their damage. \n\nThis system successfully delivers a drug past biotransport limits into a growing tumor, without need for tumor-specific \"homing\". \n\nThis simulation took a few hours to design, and ran in about 12 minutes on a desktop workstation, with data saved once per simulated minute. (2018).\nhttps://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005991\n\nThis is a PhysiCell demo of immune cells (red) attacking a 3-D heterogeneous tumor, using a basic biophysical model of an adaptive immune response to a tumor. In the simulation:\n1) Cancer cells each have an individual expression of a mutant oncoprotein, which drives proliferation. Yellow cells divide faster (lots of oncoprotein) than blue ones (very little oncoprotein).\n2) If the tumor gets too big, it outstrips the nutrient supply and a necrotic core (dead center) forms.\n3) As a simple model, tumor cells release an immunostimulatory factor that diffuses outward. Cells are assumed to have immunogenicity proportional to the mutant oncoprotein (e.g., by altering MHC with mutant peptides).\n4) At 14 days, we introduce 7500 immune cells (red) which perform a biased random walk towards the immunostimulatory factor.\n5) Whenever an immune cell touches another cell, it:\n.. a) adheres to the cell\n.. b) checks for immunogenicity\n.. c) induces apoptosis in the tumor cell at a rate proportional to immunogenicity)\n.. d) detaches either after a random time or after inducing apoptosis in the tumor cell\n6) Immune cells break away from newly apoptotic cells (cyan) and continue to seek more targets.\nThe simulation took about 2 days on a quad-core desktop (i7-4770k), including time spent on saving simulation data once every 3 simulated minutes. Simulations with less frequent output are substantially faster.\n\nLegend:\nBlue cells: tumor cells with oncoprotein &lt; 0.5\nYellow cells: tumor cells with oncoprotein &gt; 1.5\nIn between: tumor cells with 0.5 &lt; oncoprotein &lt; 1.5\n(yellow is greater)\nDark dots: cell nuclei\nCyan cells: apoptotic tumor cells\nBrown cells: necrotic tumor cells and debris\nRed cells: attacking immune cells.\n\nThis work is based on PhysiCell, an open source 3-D modeling package for multicellular biology at http://PhysiCell.MathCancer.org.\n\nMethod: \nDemonstration of PhysiCell, an agent-based, lattice-free model. Ahmadreza Ghaffarizadeh et al (2018), PLoS Comput Biol https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005991\n\nMany multicellular systems problems can only be understood by studying how cells move, grow, divide, interact, and die. Tissue-scale dynamics emerge from systems of many interacting cells as they respond to and influence their microenvironment. The ideal \u201cvirtual laboratory\u201d for such multicellular systems simulates both the biochemical microenvironment (the \u201cstage\u201d) and many mechanically and biochemically interacting cells (the \u201cplayers\u201d upon the stage). PhysiCell\u2014physics-based multicellular simulator\u2014is an open source agent-based simulator that provides both the stage and the players for studying many interacting cells in dynamic tissue microenvironments. It builds upon a multi-substrate biotransport solver to link cell phenotype to multiple diffusing substrates and signaling factors. It includes biologically-driven sub-models for cell cycling, apoptosis, necrosis, solid and fluid volume changes, mechanics, and motility \u201cout of the box.\u201d The C++ code has minimal dependencies, making it simple to maintain and deploy across platforms. PhysiCell has been parallelized with OpenMP, and its performance scales linearly with the number of cells. Simulations up to 105-106 cells are feasible on quad-core desktop workstations; larger simulations are attainable on single HPC compute nodes. We demonstrate PhysiCell by simulating the impact of necrotic core biomechanics, 3-D geometry, and stochasticity on the dynamics of hanging drop tumor spheroids and ductal carcinoma in situ (DCIS) of the breast. We demonstrate stochastic motility, chemical and contact-based interaction of multiple cell types, and the extensibility of PhysiCell with examples in synthetic multicellular systems (a \u201ccellular cargo delivery\u201d system, with application to anti-cancer treatments), cancer heterogeneity, and cancer immunology. PhysiCell is a powerful multicellular systems simulator that will be continually improved with new capabilities and performance improvements. It also represents a significant independent code base for replicating results from other simulation platforms.\n\nGood channel: https://www.youtube.com/Dlium\nSubscribe, like and comment.\n\nGood website: https://www.dlium.com\nBookmark, subscribe and comment.", "defaultAudioLanguage": "en"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT2M22S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "772", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "9", "dislikeCount": "1"}, "id": "8mE32DRYZQY"}], "idx_paper": "10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005991", "q": "10.1371/journal.pcbi.1005991"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Paul Macklin", "channelId": "UCsWaSZZzu2IrACcv1_7S0BA", "title": "PhysiCell demo: heterogeneous tumor growth", "tags": ["PhysiCell", "heterogeneity", "cancer", "cancer simulation", "selection", "evolution", "agent-based model", "ABM", "MathCancer", "multicellular", "open source", "Macklin"], "publishedAt": "2017-08-31T20:16:08Z", "description": "This is Video S7 in Ghaffarizadeh et al. Tan, Xuan Hien Bui, and Hirotaka Sato, An Ultralightweight and Living Legged Robot, Soft Robotics\nhttp://online.liebertpub.com/doi/abs/10.1089/soro.2017.0038\n\"In this study, we describe the most ultralightweight living legged robot to date that makes it a strong candidate for a search and rescue mission. The robot is a living beetle with a wireless electronic backpack stimulator mounted on its thorax. Inheriting from the living insect, the robot employs a compliant body made of soft actuators, rigid exoskeletons, and flexure hinges. Such structure would allow the robot to easily adapt to any complex terrain due to the benefit of soft interface, self-balance, and self-adaptation of the insect without any complex controller. The antenna stimulation enables the robot to perform not only left/right turning but also backward walking and even cessation of walking. We were also able to grade the turning and backward walking speeds by changing the stimulation frequency. The power required to drive the robot is low as the power consumption of the antenna stimulation is in the order of hundreds of microwatts. "UCsPffdQ-T_8p325324Sd7VA", "title": "Women\u2019s involvement in family firms: Progress and challenges for future research", "tags": ["Family business", "Women\u2019s involvement", "Gender", "Literature review", "Future research", "Giovanna Campopiano", "Alfredo De Massis", "Francesca Romana Rinaldi", "Salvatore Sciascia"], "publishedAt": "2017-12-13T09:18:21Z", "description": "Campopiano, G., De Massis, A., Rinaldi, F.R., Sciascia, S. (2017). Women\u2019s involvement in family firms: Progress and challenges for future research. Journal of Family Business Strategy, 8(4), 200-212. DOI: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jfbs.2017.09.001\n \nAvailable at: https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1877858517300578\n\nThis article reviews research on women\u2019s involvement in family firms according to a drivers-behaviors-outcomes framework. Through a systematic review, we analyze and organize the content of 87 academic articles according to the type of involvement of women in family business, i.e. entrepreneurial entry, succession, career dynamics, and presence in family firms. We identify the drivers and outcomes of women\u2019s involvement in family firms at the firm, family, and individual level of analysis, as well as the contextual factors that may influence the aforementioned elements. Drawing on these findings, we identify relevant research gaps, propose a number of future research directions aimed at bridging these gaps, and suggest unexplored research avenues.", "defaultAudioLanguage": "en"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT6M39S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "202", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "0", "dislikeCount": "1"}, "id": "Tw2nGweyF2Y"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.future.2017.09.001", "q": "10.1016/j.future.2017.09.001"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "EnergyScitechCom", "channelId": "UCSjmhIUju8bG4uWznPpHqCw", "title": "New Treatment Causes Cancer to Self Destruct - scitechdaily.com", "tags": ["Albert Einstein College Of Medicine", "Biochemistry", "Cancer", "Health", "Medicine", "Inforevolution", "Arpacolanews", "OCTOBER 9", "2017"], "publishedAt": "2017-10-10T18:11:32Z", "description": "This image depicts the structure of the BAX protein (purple). The activator compound BTSA1 (orange) has bound to the active site of BAX (green), changing the shape of the BAX molecule at several points (shown in yellow, magenta and cyan). BAX, once in its final activated form, can home in on mitochondria and puncture their outer membranes, triggering apoptosis (cell death). Credit: Albert Einstein College of Medicine\n\nA team of researchers at the Albert Einstein College of Medicine reveals the first compound that directly makes cancer cells commit suicide while sparing healthy cells. The new treatment approach was directed against acute myeloid leukemia (AML) cells but may also have potential for attacking other types of cancers.\n\n\u201cWe\u2019re hopeful that the targeted compounds we\u2019re developing will prove more effective than current anti-cancer therapies by directly causing cancer cells to self-destruct,\u201d says Evripidis Gavathiotis, Ph.D., associate professor of biochemistry and of medicine and senior author of the study. \u201cIdeally, our compounds would be combined with other treatments to kill cancer cells faster and more efficiently\u2013and with fewer adverse effects, which are an all-too-common problem with standard chemotherapies.\u201d\n\nAML accounts for nearly one-third of all new leukemia cases and kills more than 10,000 Americans each year. The survival rate for patients has remained at about 30 percent for several decades, so better treatments are urgently needed.\n\nThe newly discovered compound combats cancer by triggering apoptosis\u2013an important process that rids the body of unwanted or malfunctioning cells. Apoptosis trims excess tissue during embryonic development, for example, and some chemotherapy drugs indirectly induce apoptosis by damaging DNA in cancer cells.\n\nApoptosis occurs when BAX\u2013the \u201cexecutioner protein\u201d in cells\u2013is activated by \u201cpro-apoptotic\u201d proteins in the cell. Once activated, BAX molecules home in on and punch lethal holes in mitochondria, the parts of cells that produce energy. But all too often, cancer cells manage to prevent BAX from killing them. They ensure their survival by producing copious amounts of \u201canti-apoptotic\u201d proteins that suppress BAX and the proteins that activate it.\n\n\u201cOur novel compound revives suppressed BAX molecules in cancer cells by binding with high affinity to BAX\u2019s activation site,\u201d says Dr. Gavathiotis. \u201cBAX can then swing into action, killing cancer cells while leaving healthy cells unscathed.\u201d\n\nDr. Gavathiotis was the lead author of a 2008 paper in Nature that first described the structure and shape of BAX\u2019s activation site. He has since looked for small molecules that can activate BAX strongly enough to overcome cancer cells\u2019 resistance to apoptosis. His team initially used computers to screen more than one million compounds to reveal those with BAX-binding potential. The most promising 500 compounds\u2013many of them newly synthesized by Dr. Gavathiotis\u2019 team\u2013were then evaluated in the laboratory.\n\n\u201cA compound dubbed BTSA1 (short for BAX Trigger Site Activator 1) proved to be the most potent BAX activator, causing rapid and extensive apoptosis when added to several different human AML cell lines,\u201d says lead author Denis Reyna, M.S., a doctoral student in Dr. Gavathiotis\u2019 lab. The researchers next tested BTSA1 in blood samples from patients with high-risk AML. Strikingly, BTSA1 induced apoptosis in the patients\u2019 AML cells but did not affect patients\u2019 healthy blood-forming stem cells.\n\nFinally, the researchers generated animal models of AML by grafting human AML cells into mice. BTSA1 was given to half the AML mice while the other half served as controls. On average, the BTSA1-treated mice survived significantly longer (55 days) than the control mice (40 days), with 43 percent of BTSA1-treated AML mice alive after 60 days and showing no signs of AML.\n\nImportantly, the mice treated with BTSA1 showed no evidence of toxicity. \u201cBTSA1 activates BAX and causes apoptosis in AML cells while sparing healthy cells and tissues\u2013probably because the cancer cells are primed for apoptosis,\u201d says Dr. Gavathiotis. He notes that his study found that AML cells from patients contained significantly higher BAX levels compared with normal blood cells from healthy people. \u201cWith more BAX available in AML cells,\u201d he explained, \u201ceven low BTSA1 doses will trigger enough BAX activation to cause apoptotic death, while sparing healthy cells that contain low levels of BAX or none at all.\u201d\n\nPlans call for Dr. Gavathiotis and his team to see whether BTSA1 will show similar effectiveness when tested on animal models of other types of cancer.\n\nPublication: Denis E. "description": "On today\u2019s episode, Dr. Nick talks about different types of exercise and how each one can benefit the brain. There are many different types of exercise like low-intensity, high-intensity, aerobic/cardio, resistance and strength training, and yoga and Pilates. All of these have been shown to improve brain health by increasing blood flow, improving neuroplasticity, and strengthening brain circuits. While a certain type may be recommended for a specific disease or condition, they all can be beneficial. For general brain health, Dr. Nick thinks that you should be well-rounded and diverse in your exercise routine. This keeps the body guessing and prevents boredom, avoids over-training in one area or one part of the body, and improves all aspects of mental, emotional, and physical health. Check out the video for more in depth information on the benefits of exercise for the brain and how to set up a weekly exercise schedule!\n\nSchmitt A, Upadhyay N, Martin JA, Rojas S, Str\u00fcder HK, and Boecker H. Face detection is a difficult task in image analysis which has each day more and more applications. In fact, the object \u201cface\u201d is hard to define because of its large variability, depending on the identity of the person, the lighting conditions, the psychological context of the person, etc.\n\nThe main challenge for detecting faces is to find a classifier which can discriminate faces from all other possible images.  The existing methods for face detection can be divided into image-based methods and feature-based methods. We have developed an intermediate system, using a Haar classifier-based algorithm and Curvelet based feature extraction which is capable of processing images rapidly with having good detection rates. The main idea in the Haar transformation algorithm is the discrete wavelet transformation of an image using haar coefficients to locate the maximum wavelet region which represents the face location. This improves both, the detection speed and the detection efficiency.  Whereas in split the total image into a small block (5X5) and apply the convolution process between each block and curvelet coefficient and find the features of all the image blocks.\n\nHAAR CLASSIFIER \nImage is converted to text format by using Matlab tool then apply haar construction to locate wavelet maximum region which is nothing but a face, after computation of the face location by using haar coefficients then haar reconstruction to retain the original image with located face regions. After the eddies cross the Walvis Ridge (between 0 and 5E), the number of particles retained increases and the ones that are lost tend to follow the westward movement of the eddies. My focus is on specific \u2018movements\u2019 or \u2018turns\u2019 in tourism research rather than on discrete topics or subject areas. My central argument is that these \u2018turns\u2019 have pushed beyond traditional research frontiers and have thus transformed the way we think about and do tourism. Three \u2018turns\u2019 are briefly discussed \u2013 the critical turn, the postdisciplinary turn and the mobilities turn. I conclude with a call for tourism researchers to avoid knowledges which are produced via the easy path of imitation, and instead to embrace the bitter and noble routes to the creation of tourism knowledges which stem from our own reflections and experiences of being in tourism.\n\nAccess the article at: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.010"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M58S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "127", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "1", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "7tV9IdEt8gE"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.010", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.010"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Sociedad Espa\u00f1ola de Cardiolog\u00eda", "channelId": "UCsySMJfKVnZZudEJCKy8wHA", "title": "Ablaci\u00f3n pedi\u00e1trica: caracter\u00edsticas y resultados en un centro de referencia. Understanding resilience and crisis management in tourism\nGirish Prayag\n\nAbstract: This opinion piece argues the need for researchers to shift to resilience rather than crisis management research in tourism studies. While the two concepts are inherently linked, existing studies prioritize the latter rather than the former. Also, a strong focus on disasters as the backdrop for resilience research in tourism is highlighted. I argue that both fast and slow paced changes that impact the tourism system and conceptual issues with respect to concepts such as destination resilience must be studied. I highlight several gaps in the tourism literature on resilience and offer avenues for further research. Specifically, the need for research on destination resilience, psychological resilience, employee resilience and organizational resilience is emphasized.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.012\n\n--\n\nReflections to move forward: Where destination crisis management research needs to go\nLori Pennington-Gray\n\nAbstract: The frequency and fury of crises have flourished over the past decade. Globally, we are faced with more crises and disasters that ever before. The need for quality academic research is at an all-time high. More scholarly approaches to problems, greater theoretical foundations for studies, fewer case studies, more longitudinal research, and more comparative studies will help advance the destination crisis management scholarship while, at the same time, aiding the industry to mitigate crises both prior to as well as during times of need.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.013"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M16S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "396", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "1", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "iTTrywP9EHU"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"title": "Jornada de exposici\u00f3n articulo cient\u00edfico 2020-2 UCO", "publishedAt": "2020-05-16T22:09:38Z", "channelTitle": "Duvan Felipe Gonzalez Castrillon", "channelId": "UCil0kD5PjWbgFreEcjlc-7w", "description": "Ponentes:\nCesar Augusto Echeverri Echeverri.\nDuvan Felipe Gonzalez Castrillon.\nJos\u00e9 Davian Arenas Montoya.\n\nAsignatura:\nIngenier\u00eda econ\u00f3mica y financiera.\n\nArticulo: \nEconomic-financial performance of the Brazilian sugarcane energy industry: An empirical evaluation using financial ratio, cluster and discriminant analysis (https://doi.org/10.1016/j.biombioe.2017.11.013)\n\nDocente y asesora:\nMar\u00eda Victoria Silva Dom\u00ednguez."}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT12M48S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "17", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "0", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "4zzeyUgupOg"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Alexandros G. Sfakianakis,Anapafseos 5 Agios Nikolaos 72100 Crete Greece,00302841026182,00306932607174,alsfakia@gmail.com,\r\nhttps://plus.google.com/communities/115462130054650919641?sqinv=VFJWaER0c2NCRl9ERzRjZWhxQmhzY09kVV84cjRn\r\n,\r\n,https://plus.google.com/u/0/+AlexandrosGSfakianakis\r\n,\r\nhttps://www.youtube.com/channel/UCQH21WX8Qn5YSTKrlJ3OrmQ\r\n,\r\nhttps://www.youtube.com/channel/UCTREJHxB6yt4Gaqs4-mLzDA\r\n,\r\nhttps://twitter.com/g_orl?lang=el,\r\nhttps://www.instagram.com/alexandrossfakianakis/,\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nArticle in Press\r\nReliability and Validity of the Turkish Version of the Consensus Auditory-Perceptual Evaluation of Voice (CAPE-V)\r\nEsra \u00d6zcebe'Correspondence information about the author Esra \u00d6zcebeEmail the author Esra \u00d6zcebe, Fatma Esen Aydinli, Tu\u011f\u00e7e Karahan Ti\u011frak, \u00d6nal \u0130ncebay, Taner Yilmaz\r\nDOI: http://dx.doi.org/10.1016/j.jvoice.2017.11.013\r\nshowArticle Info\r\nAbstract\r\nFull Text\r\nReferences\r\nSupplemental Materials\r\nSummary\r\nObjectives\r\nThe main purpose of this study was to culturally adapt the Consensus Auditory-Perceptual Evaluation of Voice (CAPE-V) to Turkish and to evaluate its internal consistency, validity, and reliability.\r\n\r\nMaterials and Methods\r\nThe Turkish version of CAPE-V was developed, and with the use of a prospective case-control design, the voice recordings of 130 participants were collected according to CAPE-V protocol. Auditory-perceptual evaluation was conducted according to CAPE-V and Grade, Roughness, Breathiness, Asthenia, and Strain (GRBAS) scale by two ear, nose, and throat specialists and two speech and language therapists. The different types of voice disorders, classified as organic and functional disorders, were compared in terms of their CAPE-V scores.\r\n\r\nResults\r\nThe overall severity parameter had the highest intrarater and inter-reliability values for all the participants. For all four raters, the differences in the six CAPE-V parameters between the study and the control groups were found to be statistically significant. Among the correlations for the comparable parameters of the CAPE-V and the GRBAS scales, the highest correlation was found between the overall severity-grade parameters. There was no difference found between the organic and functional voice disorders in terms of the CAPE-V scores.\r\n\r\nConclusions\r\nThe Turkish version of CAPE-V has been proven to be a reliable and valid instrument to use in the auditory-perceptual evaluation of voice. For the future application of this study, it would be important to investigate whether cepstral measures correlate with the auditory-perceptual judgments of dysphonia severity collected by a Turkish version of the CAPE-V.\r\n\r\nKey Words:\r\nAuditory-perceptual assessment, CAPE-V, GRBAS, Dysphonia, Voice quality\n\r\n\r- video upload powered by https://www.TunesToTube.com"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT2M16S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "1771", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "0", "dislikeCount": "2"}, "id": "LH4hVF2nXSE"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.013"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Pamela Beatrice Getalado", "channelId": "UCg3BHkndN-8UrbqiSd-2Bzg", "title": "Let's Talk about Livestreaming... // NETS2000 // Reflective Web Media Creation (Draft)", "tags": ["fan culture", "livestream", "concerts", "digitisation", "non-commercial"], "publishedAt": "2020-05-29T02:10:25Z", "description": "Today's vlog will be talking about how livestreams have digitised the music industry and the concert scene. https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/tourism-management-perspectives/vol/25/suppl/C\n\n\nNew technologies in tourism: From multi-disciplinary to anti-disciplinary advances and trajectories\nMarianna Sigala\n\nAbstract: Technologies transform tourism management and marketing from a static and utilitarian sense (whereby managers and tourists use technologies as tools) to a transformative conceptualization whereby tourism markets and actors both shape and are shaped by technology. This paper unravels the transformative power of technologies on: the tourism actors and resources (both the traditional but also new actors, i.e. the technology agents); the ways actors interact to (co-)create but also (co-)destruct tourism value; and the context in which tourism actors interact from a linear supply chain tourism \u2018industry\u2019 to a complex socio-technical smart tourism ecosystem. To study such complex phenomena and transformations, the paper emphasises that research should not only adopt a multi-disciplinary approach, but it also needs to follow an anti-disciplinary thinking whereby new knowledge and constructs do not simply fall within existing paradigms, disciplinary silos and mindsets once developed by studying the \u2018pure\u2019 humans and their behaviours.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.12.003\n\n--\n\nFrom digitization to the age of acceleration: On information technology and tourism\nPhil Xiang\n\nAbstract: This essay presents an overview of the research development over the last twenty years on information technology and tourism. It argues that knowledge created in the last two decades can be characterized as consisting of two distinct eras, i.e., Digitization (1997\u20132006) and Age of Acceleration (2007\u20132016), which reflected the general understanding of how technology has transformed our society and economy. Knowledge development within each of these eras is examined in terms of the technological conditions, dominant paradigms, main research questions, and influential discipline and research approaches. Particularly, it recognizes the shift of our view of information technology in tourism research from a primarily a marketing-driven tool to a knowledge creation tool due to new technological conditions such as the smartphone, drone, wearables, new connectivity and big data. Finally, this essay discusses possible future research problems and challenges our existing views of the relationship between information technology and tourism.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.023"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M10S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "253", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "2", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "i5rS_UTRcYc"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"title": "ED = ED = ED : ERECTILE, ENDOTHELIAL, EMOTIONAL DYSFUNCTION", "publishedAt": "2020-07-19T06:13:52Z", "channelTitle": "OneMD", "channelId": "UCty6V7qeaU45JGmjYzzYdlA", "description": ""}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1H31M51S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "3", "viewCount": "1294", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "71", "dislikeCount": "3"}, "id": "wUHBFp5PQpE", "liveStreamingDetails": {"actualStartTime": "2020-07-19T04:30:34Z"}}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Sociedad Espa\u00f1ola de Cardiolog\u00eda", "channelId": "UCsySMJfKVnZZudEJCKy8wHA", "title": "Grasa epic\u00e1rdica y muerte s\u00fabita cardiaca isqu\u00e9mica. The authors conducted a search to identify scientific papers. The titles and abstracts were analyzed regarding word frequency and relations between them, through hierarchical cluster analysis and co-occurrence networks. The frequency of journals was calculated, as well as the amount of papers across time.\r\n\r\nResults\r\nSince 1949, 754 papers were published and an increase was noticed. Even though 162 journals were identified by the authors, the Journal of Voice holds the majority of papers, in every analyzed period. An evolution of studied topics is described. Up to 2010, the main theme was professional singers, especially classical and opera interpreters. Since then, voice quality and the effects of training gathered more attention.\r\n\r\nConclusions\r\nThe growing interest in singing has been conspicuous since the first indexed paper. However, it has been slightly slowing down. Until 2010, great importance was given to the voice quality of singers and their occupational demands. Acoustic analysis was widely used to study the effects of training. Since 2010, the concern with functionality is increasing, rather than the organic voice structures. Musical perception studies have been a trend, as well as the use of electroglottography.\r\n\r\nKey Words:\r\nSinging, Voice, Clustering, Text mining, Scientometry\n\r\n\r- video upload powered by https://www.TunesToTube.com"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT2M16S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "6", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "0", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "7be-49uYSds"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.12.003"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "gemvideoproduction", "channelId": "UC3Imqe1xm7j7_8y5o2pfyHA", "title": "Biotech Robots for Babies", "tags": ["Biotech", "science", "baby", "babies", "robots", "University of Delaware", "Newark", "Doctor", "Dr. Cole Galloway", "Sunil Agrawal", "Spina Bifida", "Cerebral Palsy"], "publishedAt": "2011-04-06T20:52:59Z", "description": "James C. However, the classic features are readily provided by patients during history taking. Migraine-associated dizziness and vertigo is a common mimicker of Meniere Disease which can also be managed initially by the family physician, with consideration given to a referral to neurology or neurotology (subspecialty of otolaryngology). As peripheral vestibular disorders are uncommon causes of attacks of dizziness and patient-reported vertigo, the first step in the approach to patients with dizziness or vertigo is delineating between true vertigo and other causes of dizziness. Treatment of Meniere's Disease ranges from conservative through nonablative to occasionally ablative therapies. Conservative therapy with nursing begins with diet modification and betahistine, which can be initiated by the family physician. Referral to an otolaryngologist is recommended for all patients suspected of having Meniere Disease. Most patients with Meniere's Disease obtain good control of their symptoms with exercises, personalized treatment and management.\n\n\nReference:\nKoenen L, Andaloro C. Meniere Disease. This paper describes a simple and versatile approach to produce ceramics with porosity gradient. In order to perform this study, MnO2/SnO2 bi-layered pellets were conformed via uniaxial pressure and sintered at 1100 degrees C and 1300 degrees C for different times. MnO2 layer had the role of sintering aid, while the SnO2 layer was chosen as ceramic matrix subjected to the densification. The field emission scanning electron microscope (FE-SEM) was employed to obtain information on the micro structural features of these pellets. FE-SEM micrographs revealed that the overall percentage of porosity, pore size and shape in SnO2 layer can be controlled by sintering variables (temperature and time). The subsequent outbreaks after 2013 throughout the world had finally\ntransformed the Zika disease as Public Health Emergency of International Concern (PhEIC)\nin Feb 2016 and further the spread got under control by late 2017 [1]. Acquiring a mosquito\nbased and sexual mode of transmissions, the actual threat posed by ZIKV is associated with\nneurological defects like microcephaly and Guillain-Barre syndrome in new-borns as well as\nin adults respectively [2]. The speaker will discuss his research on Zika virus proteins from\nstructure\u2013function and inhibitor discovery perspective. In general, the viruses have very\nlimited number of proteins. In case of Zika virus, it encodes ten proteins: three structural\nand seven nonstructural proteins. Additionally, there are two small peptides as well, such as,\nPeptide 2K & Capsid Anchor. To begin with, we have raised a fundamental question that how\nthese limited set of Zika proteins acquire multifunctional capabilities such that these can\nhijack the host system and induce the disease efficiently. Taking advantage from literature,\nwe have found a strong correlation of intrinsically disordered proteins with multifunctional\ncapabilities which was also shown to be highly implicated in viral proteomes [3]. Therefore,\nbased upon these studies, we have raised few questions to elucidate the molecular basis of Zika virus disease. What is the intrinsic disorder propensity in Zika virus? What are the\nbiophysical properties of important enzymatic proteins of Zika virus in terms of folding and\nfunctioning? How does intrinsic flexibility of Zika virus proteins implicated in viral replication\nand propagation? In order to answer all these questions, we have firstly studied the role\nof intrinsic disorder in the maturation of proteins of Zika virus [4]. Further, in NS2B-NS3\nprotease, we proved experimentally that the NS2B cofactor region of the viral protease is\nintrinsically disordered in nature [5]. In fact, this is the case of disorder\u2013function\u2013paradigm.\nAnother case is N-terminal Capsid region (1\u201330 residues), which folds upon binding to lipids\nand uses the disorder\u2013function\u2013paradigm for remodelling the host membranes. Additionally,\nwe also performed the inhibitor discovery experiments and found that Hydroxychloroquine\ninhibits the Zika virus protease activity [6]. Another finding of inhibitor discovery includes\nthe Helicase enzyme inhibition by green tea molecule EGCG [7].\n\nReferences:\n[1] L.R. Petersen, D.J. Jamieson, A.M. This video hopes to bring attention to the severity of this issue. Warming temperatures as a result of climate change are causing tick populations to sky-rocket and with more ticks comes more disease. Specifically, the increase in black-legged tick/deer tick (ixodes scapularis) population results in the increased prevalence of Lyme disease. "description": "Everyone is curious, but not everyone is curious in the same way\n\nwww.instagram.com/everwonderedyt\nwww.twitter.com/everwonderedyt\nwww.patreon.com/everwonderedyt\nwww.facebook.com/everwonderedyt\n\nReferences:\n\n\nKashdan, T., Stiksma, M., Disabato, D., Journal of Research and Personality. 73, 130-149. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jrp.2017.11.011\n\nKidd, C. & Hayden, B. (2015). The psychology and Neuroscience of curiosity. Neuron Perspective. 88. (3), 449-460. doi: 10.1016/j.neuron.2015.09.010\n\nEver wondered which kind of curious person are you?\n\nA 2018 study found that roughly speaking there are 4 groups of curious people.\n\nFirst is the fascinated group. This group has persons with inquisitive and usually positive mindsets. \n\nThese fascinated persons are social, assertive and want to know more. Because of this it is likely that they have a lot of passions and interests. Also fascinated people usually see life as an adventure, and just so you know, these fascinated persons usually make more money and have more friends and followers on social media.\n\nThe fascinated group is thought to be approximately 28% of the population\n\nAlso representing 28% of the population is the second group, the Problem Solvers group. Problem solvers are hard-working individuals that love to learn while working relentlessly and they feel that every problem should be solved. \n\nProblem solvers prefer to work in well solving problems and seeking information. They are very independent, and usually show less interest in accessing social media and understanding people.\n\nAlso problem solvers usually see life as a mission to uncover something specific in their lives.\n\nThird group is The Empathizers . Curiosity has even been related to a higher probability of pleasurable and meaningful moments in life\n\nHowever there are four dimensions of curiosity. The first one is perceptual curiosity. Perceptual curiosity is triggered by a novel, surprising or puzzling stimuli. So when you see something odd and you want to take a closer look. Perceptually curious people usually want to experience something new through the senses. \n\n\nFor example the first time you experience snow, and just so you know the first time I experienced snow was when I was 28 years old so I had a lot of perceptual curiosity. Also perceptual curiosity generally diminishes with continued exposure to the same stimuli, for example the time I got bored of the snow within 15 minutes of touching it for the first time.\n\n\nSecond is Epistemic curiosity, which is the desire for new knowledge. Epistemic curiosity is the desire to know \u201cwhy?\u201d or \u201cwhat if?\u201d . This type of curiosity it\u2019s the one that comes to your mind when you think about curious people. There is much greater need for policy relevant research that is clear about common definitions of terminology, adopts more consistent methodologies in data collection, challenges the dominant pro-growth rhetoric, and is written in a style accessible to policymakers. Researchers have long argued for a more meaningful role for host communities, but in a time of rapidly increasing tourism and the threat of overtourism in many destination \u201chot spots\u201d, it is no longer an option to stifle their voices.\n\nDecisions related to goal-determination and the selection of methods to achieve the goal are referred to as policies. Although the term generally refers to a decision or action, it actually can also be a negative decision or even a non-action/non-decision. Policies are established in any kind of organization, but when we refer to \u201ctourism policy\u201d, we usually mean some form of \u201cpublic policy\u201d which relates specifically to government decisions at any level from local to international. Governance, on the other hand, is how organizations deal with reaching these decisions. So, while governance is a fairly straightforward concept, albeit with many challenges, tourism policy is not, largely because the term \u201cpolicy\u201d is very fuzzy and tourism is a social construct that refers to a specific behavior: that of traveling to and staying in places outside one's usual environment. This behavior is controlled by policies, legislation and regulations written for many other purposes, such as controlling or facilitating the flow of capital and investments, the transportation of passengers and goods, worker rights, safety and security, or environmental protection. And that's where the trouble starts, because really, the appropriate development of tourism is highly dependent on decision-makers who have little regard for or knowledge of, tourism.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.011"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT59S"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "377", "favoriteCount": "0", "likeCount": "3", "dislikeCount": "0"}, "id": "cbkRhLAOgJw"}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.011", "q": "10.1016/j.media.2017.11.011"}, {"items": [{"snippet": {"channelTitle": "Professor Dimitrios Buhalis", "channelId": "UC9R8by0roMNwuzEyEfo7Xaw", "title": "Professor Dimitrios Buhalis contribution to #WeAreTogether by INOMO on COVID Impacts to Tourism", "publishedAt": "2020-04-04T22:48:21Z", "description": "Professor Dimitrios Buhalis contribution to #WeAreTogether by INOMO in conversation with Vivian Paraschou and Kyros Asfis on COVID Impacts to Tourism and Hospitality Saturday 4th March 2020.  \nhttps://youtu.be/PyAiRcu26bA \n\nInvited by Vivian Paraschou and Kyros Asfis on the #WeAreTogether initiative by INOMO to talk about COVID Impacts to Tourism. Understanding resilience and crisis management in tourism\nGirish Prayag\n\nAbstract: This opinion piece argues the need for researchers to shift to resilience rather than crisis management research in tourism studies. While the two concepts are inherently linked, existing studies prioritize the latter rather than the former. Also, a strong focus on disasters as the backdrop for resilience research in tourism is highlighted. I argue that both fast and slow paced changes that impact the tourism system and conceptual issues with respect to concepts such as destination resilience must be studied. I highlight several gaps in the tourism literature on resilience and offer avenues for further research. Specifically, the need for research on destination resilience, psychological resilience, employee resilience and organizational resilience is emphasized.\n\nAccess: https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tmp.2017.11.012\n\n--\n\nReflections to move forward: Where destination crisis management research needs to go\nLori Pennington-Gray\n\nAbstract: The frequency and fury of crises have flourished over the past decade. We studied the clinical course to explore appropriate treatment strategies. We retrospectively studied consecutive 33 patients who had CSC-HE. The disease stage was classified into 4 groups: group A, early head and neck cancer (HNC) and early esophageal cancer (EC); group B, early HNC and advanced EC; group C, advanced HNC and early EC; and group D, advanced HNC and advanced EC. As induction chemotherapy, the patients received 3 courses of TPF therapy (docetaxel 75mg/m 2 on day 1, cisplatin 75mg/m 2 on day 1, and 5-fluorouracil 750mg/m 2 on days 1-5) at 3-week intervals. The clinical courses and treatment outcomes were studied according to the disease stage of CSC-HE. The disease stage of CSC-HE was group A in 1 patient (3%), group B in 9 patients (27.3%), group C in 3 patients (9.1%), and group D in 20 patients (60.6%). The median follow-up was 26months, and the 2-year overall survival rate was 67.4%. In groups A, B, and C, the 2-year overall survival rate was 83.3%. In group D, the 2-year overall survival rate was 62.6%. Ten of 20 patients in group D received induction chemotherapy with TPF, and 6 patients were alive and disease free at the time of this writing. The treatment outcomes of patients with CSC-HE were relatively good. TPF induction chemotherapy might be an effective treatment for patients with advanced HNC and advanced EC. Copyright \u00a9 2018.
